<h1>Website Title</h1>: Main heading, typically used once per page.

<h2>About Us</h2>: Subheading under the main section.

<h3>Team Members</h3>: Further subsection within a previous heading level. ^F695mnUI

Opening tag: <h1> through <h6>

Text content

Closing tag: </h1> through </h6> ^bT0vygiE

Using headings out of order (e.g., jumping from <h1> to <h4>)

Using headings for styling rather than semantics

Including multiple <h1> tags improperly (acceptable in HTML5 if semantically justified)

Omitting headings altogether, leading to poor accessibility and SEO ^5tzZLpuy

Heading vs Paragraph (<p>): A heading indicates structural level; a paragraph represents content flow.

<h1> vs <title>: <h1> is visible content in <body>; <title> is metadata in <head>.

Headings are not chosen for styling but for semantic meaning. ^uF9ogIVh

A heading in HTML is a semantic element used to define the hierarchical structure and organization of content within a web page. HTML provides six levels of headings, represented by the tags <h1> through <h6>, where <h1> indicates the highest or most important level, and <h6> the lowest. Each heading element introduces a new section or subsection, and search engines and assistive technologies use this hierarchy to interpret document structure, navigate content, and assign weight to titles for indexing or accessibility purposes. Headings do not alter document logic beyond visual and semantic organization and must be used sequentially and meaningfully to preserve structural integrity. ^BMqQwy3V

Distinctions ^u7KtDXw5
